SUBJECT:
Enterprise Resource Planning System Replacement Project – Change Order C03
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Change Order C03 to the agreement with Collaborative Solutions for extending the Phase II timeline by an 
additional 14 weeks for the enterprise resource planning system replacement project in the amount of $260,235, for a 
new Phase II total of $1,503,375 and a new agreement total of $2,866,895.
BACKGROUND:
The City Council awarded contract to Collaborative Solutions (Collaborative) in February 2022 as a part of the enterprise 
resource planning (ERP) system replacement project in the amount of $2,527,160. Implementation is in phases, with Phase 
I covering the core financial elements, including accounting, accounts payable, accounts receivable, and financial 
reporting. Phase I began in March 2022 and went live on November 1, 2022. The City Council approved Change Order C01 
on November 7, 2022 in the amount of $14,700. Change Order C02 is also on the same Council meeting agenda under a 
separate item, as the change in scope is for Phase I of the ERP implementation, which implemented Workday Financials.
Phase II of the ERP implementation, which began implementation efforts on October 10, 2022, will deliver Workday 
payroll, time keeping, and human capital management (HCM) functionality to the City. Based on information that was 
yielded as a part of the Architect Stage interviews, Order C03 is for the cost of increasing the overall timeline from 44 
weeks to 58 weeks of Phase II. One of the primary drivers for the change order are the time keeping/scheduling solutions 
that are used by the San Mateo Police Department (SMPD) and the San Mateo Consolidated Fire Department (SMC Fire). 
During the pre-implementation scoping process, the original scope of work anticipated integrations with the time 
keeping/scheduling solutions for SMPD and SMC Fire, which included calculation of payroll within these solutions before 
the data is passed on to Workday. However, the optimal configuration will be to have the respective public safety time 
keeping solutions pass on the employee hours to the Workday ERP to calculate payroll. In order to configure Workday to 
calculate public safety payroll, additional scope and time are necessary given the complexity of public safety payroll. As a 
means of comparison, implementation of the Tyler Eden payroll and HCM modules took 130 weeks (two and a half years). 
Approval of Change Order C03 will increase the timeline for ERP Phase II from 44 weeks to 58 weeks.
During Phase II Planning and Architecture stages, the City uncovered additional Workday capabilities that will help us 
further streamline our business processes, improve efficiency, and enhance effectiveness in delivering services to our 
employees. These areas include benefit administration, compensation tracking and CalPERS reporting requirements, 
recruiting, onboarding staff, talent management, and integrations with third party vendors. Waiting to implement these 
capabilities at a later date or after go-live will cost the City more time, effort, and funds because it will require re-work and 
duplication of effort. This rework and duplication are avoided now as we are in the building stage, and this will only be 
needed to be done once. 
367 of 417

--- page 368 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Based on the City’s experience with Phase I, additional time for the testing and payroll parallel stages is critical to the 
success of Phase II to provide adequate time to test the configuration of Workday and ensure that payroll and benefits are 
correctly set up to serve the City’s most important assets – its employees. As such, Change Order C03 includes five 
additional weeks of testing and two additional weeks of payroll parallel, where payroll will be run in Tyler Eden system and 
the test tenant of the Workday solution. Absent the additional time afforded by Change Order C03, Human Resources, 
Information Technology, and Finance department staff will be put in a difficult position of validating the new Workday 
solution without adequate time to complete the task, putting the City at higher risk of more errors coming to fruition in 
the production environment. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
No supplemental budget appropriations are necessary. The cost of Change Order C03 can be offset by General Fund 
vacancy savings in the current fiscal year. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This change order is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not 
result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

SUBJECT:
Building Inspections, Permit Technician, Off-Site Plan Review, and Code Enforcement Inspection Services – Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Amendment No. 1 to the agreement with 4LEAF, Inc. for professional consultant services for building Inspections, 
permit technician, off-site plan review, and code enforcement inspection services to extend the term through January 31, 
2023, and increase the agreement amount by $161,000 for a new agreement total of $260,000. 
BACKGROUND:
On June 30, 2022, the City Manager approved an agreement with 4LEAF, Inc. for building inspection, permit technician, 
off-site plan review, and code enforcement inspection services in an amount not-to-exceed $99,000. The services 4LEAF 
provides include the review of plans, calculations, and reports for compliance with adopted building codes and the 
provision of technical advice, reports, and correspondence related to plan check services. These specialized services are 
typically provided by a structural engineer, and due to the consistently high volume of plan submittals and ongoing staff 
constraints, the Community Development Department (CDD) will exhaust the contracted amount more quickly than 
anticipated. 
This amendment will allow CDD to maintain current levels of service for the next two months. Staff are evaluating 
responses to a Request for Qualifications (RFQ) for long-term building support services and will be returning to Council in 
January 2023 with multiple contracts for review. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
The additional $161,000 in costs resulting from this amendment can be absorbed within the fiscal year 2022-23 
operational budget for the Community Development Department.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This contract amendment is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that 
will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

TO:

FROM:
Drew Corbett, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
December 05, 2022 
SUBJECT:
Marina Branch Library Improvement Project – Grant Funding
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to authorize an application for and accept funding in the amount of $458,600 from the Building 
Forward Library Infrastructure Grant Program for the Marina Branch Library Improvement Project with a commitment of 
local matching funds in the same amount; and authorize the City Manager to execute all required documents. 
BACKGROUND:
The California State Library manages the Building Forward Library Infrastructure Grant Program (Program), which provides 
public libraries with funding for capital improvements that address critical maintenance, sustainability and energy 
efficiency, and digital and physical projects that expand access. The Program is the State of California’s largest single 
investment for the public library system. In 2021, the California Legislature provided $439 million in one-time funds 
(Senate Bill 129) for the Program and an additional $50 million were provided in 2022 (Assembly Bill 179). 
 
Earlier this year, staff identified critical maintenance needs at the Marina Branch Library. The Marina Branch Library is 
located at 1530 Susan Court and has served the community since 1966. Situated on the west embankment of Seal Slough, 
the building has experienced differential settlement on the order of five inches and currently leans towards the waterway. 
As a result, the floor slopes up to 7% on the interior and has created an unsafe environment for both patrons and staff. 
 
To address the critical issues, staff developed the Marina Branch Library Improvement Project (Project) to restore the 
sloping floors to near-level conditions. Preliminary geotechnical and structural investigations indicate that the settlement 
has occurred due to consolidation of the bay mud soils for the one-story library building. The finding indicates that 40-foot-
deep concrete-filled steel tube micropiles will be required to re-level the floors. Additional improvements are also needed 
to comply with American with Disabilities Act requirements. City staff subsequently applied for $1,750,000 in grant funding 
from the Program to fund the Project.  The City was recently notified of a grant award in the amount of $458,600 from the 
Program pending final application documentation and adoption of a required resolution by the City.
 
The proposed Project is critical to ensure that the conditions at the Marina Branch Library are addressed. Staff plans to 
issue a request for proposals for the development of the design at the beginning of next year. The intent is to complete the 
design, assess the costs, and begin construction in 2024.   
BUDGET IMPACT:
The design and construction costs for the Marina Library Structural Improvements Project are estimated at $5,000,000. 
Staff applied for $1,750,000 in grant funding through the Program and Council approved $1,750,000 in general funds 
required for the 1:1 matching funding, appropriated through the fiscal year 2022-23 budget process. The City was notified 
of a Program grant award in the amount of $458,600 for the Project, pending final application documentation and a 
385 of 417

--- page 386 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
resolution. Additional funding of $1,300,000 has been awarded through the California budget surplus, as well as a pending 
$1,500,000 from an earmark in the federal budget.  Should the federal budget earmark not come to fruition, staff will 
identify additional sources of funding during the design effort. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This application for grant funding and acceptance of grant funds is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an 
organizational or administrative activity that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA 
Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)

CITY OF SAN MATEO
RESOLUTION NO. ____ (2022)
A RESOLUTION SUPPORTING THE MARINA BRANCH LIBRARY IMPROVEMENT PROJECT, SUBMISSION OF A 
GRANT APPLICATION TO THE CALIFORNIA STATE LIBRARY’S BUILDING FORWARD LIBRARY INFRASTRUCTURE 
GRANT PROGRAM, AND ACCEPTANCE AND EXECUTION OF THE GRANT FUNDS FROM THE STATE OF 
CALIFORNIA BUDGET ACT OF 2021 (SB 129)
WHEREAS, the Legislature and Governor of the State of California have provided funds for the program 
shown above; and 
WHEREAS, the California State Library has been delegated the responsibility for the administration of 
this grant program, establishing necessary procedures; and
WHEREAS, said procedures established by the California State Library require a resolution certifying the 
approval by the potential grantee’s governing board either before submission of said application(s) to the State 
or prior to execution of the grant agreement; and
WHEREAS, the City of San Mateo (City) has identified improvements estimated at $5,000,000 for the 
Marina Branch Library; and 
WHEREAS, the City has developed and proposes to implement the Marina Branch Library Improvement 
Project (Project) for the design and construction of the improvements; and 
WHEREAS, the City as the Applicant/Grantee, if selected, will enter into an agreement with the State of 
California to carry out the Project; and 
WHEREAS, the City has the legal authority and is authorized to enter into a funding agreement with the 
State of California; and
WHEREAS, the City intends to apply for grant funding from the California State Library for the Project.
NOW, THEREFORE, THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, HEREBY RESOLVES that: 
1.
Pursuant and subject to all of the terms and provisions of the California Budget Act of 2021, the City 
Manager, or designee, is authorized and directed to prepare and file an application for funding with the 
California State Library and take such other actions necessary or appropriate to obtain grant funding.
2.
The City is committed to the completion of the Project, including the appropriation of the estimated 
$458,600 in matching funds needed for implementation, if awarded the requested funds.
387 of 417

--- page 388 ---
3.
The City Manager, or designee, is authorized and directed to execute the funding agreement with the 
California State Library and any amendments thereto. 
4.
The City Manager, or designee, is authorized and directed to submit any required documents, funding 
requests, and reports required to obtain grant funding.
5.
The City certifies that the Project will comply with any laws and regulations including, but not limited to, 
the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA), legal requirements for building codes, health and 
safety codes, the California Labor Code, disabled access laws, and that prior to commencement of the 
Project, all applicable permits will have been obtained.
6.
The City Manager, or designee, is authorized to take any other actions necessary to give effect to this 
resolution.

From:
Faye Jennings
To:
Clerk; Adam Loraine; Lisa Diaz Nash; Rob Newsom; Amourence Lee
Subject:
Mayor of San Mateo
Date:
Saturday, December 3, 2022 5:59:55 PM
Dear Mayor Bonilla, Council Members Goethals, Lee, Papan, and Rodriguez, and 
Council Members-Elect Loraine, Diaz-Nash, and Newsom
I am writing in strong support of the selection of Council Member Amourence Lee as 
San Mateo's next Mayor, at the City Council meeting on December 5, 2022.  
Experience matters and only Council Member Lee has it, having served the City well 
for the last three years, after her appointment in 2019 and her election in 2020. As the 
only holdover from the most recent council, she is the only Council Member who can 
provide continuity, bringing an intimate awareness of past discussions.
The Mayor of San Mateo is an important position, setting the tone, leading the 
discussion, and representing San Mateo in numerous regional bodies.
Mayor Lee would be the first Mayor of Asian descent in the City's history.  She would 
be the first Mayor from North Central San Mateo in 20 years.
And finally, according to the City Council Handbook, Council Member Lee becomes 
Vice Mayor on December 4, with the resignation of Diane Papan from the City 
Council.  San Mateo custom has the Vice Mayor becoming the next Mayor.
Please select Council Member Amourence Lee as Mayor of San Mateo!
Thank you,
Faye Jennings
North Shoreview SMC resident

From:
Caiti Busch
To:
Clerk; Adam Loraine; Lisa Diaz Nash; Amourence Lee; Rob Newsom
Subject:
Councilmember Lee for Mayor
Date:
Sunday, December 4, 2022 9:54:12 AM
Dear Councilmember Lee, and Councilmembers-Elect Loraine, Diaz-Nash, and 
Newsom,
I am writing to urge you to select Councilmember Lee as the next Mayor of San 
Mateo. Councilmember Lee has demonstrated great commitment to our City, has the 
experience necessary for the job, values and promotes representation of all of our 
community members, and is a competent and courageous leader.
Moreover, San Mateo City Council practice and custom has long called for the 
promotion of the Vice Mayor to the Mayor position. Tomorrow night, Councilmember 
Lee will assume the Vice Mayor role, and I urge you to follow past practice and 
promote her to Mayor. Though I am not a San Mateo historian, I understand that the 
Council has long had a rotating mayor; we do not have an at-large mayor like our 
neighboring Belmont just adopted. In the absence of a democratically-elected at-large 
mayor, the rotating mayor system is incredibly important to upholding several core 
democratic principles: (1) distributing power among the Council's members; (2) 
ensuring equitable representation for those who voted for each councilmember (even 
more so now that the City is moving to District elections); (3) balancing the various, 
and at times divergent, views of our councilmembers; (4) promoting diversity by 
allowing all members to hold positions of power; and (5) insulating our council against 
partisan politics. A vote against the longstanding practice of electing the Vice Mayor 
to Mayor--no matter who they are--is, to me, a vote against these core principles. I 
would hope that I would be writing this same email to you regardless of who was 
rising to power--whether I agreed with them or not. I urge you in your first official act 
as City Council members to not revert to partisanship, and instead to demonstrate 
your dedication to working collegially with your colleagues and to representing all of 
San Mateo.
Thank you so much to all of you for your willingness to serve; I believe in you all and 
am so grateful to you.
Best,
Caiti Busch
**Disclosure: I am a member of the San Mateo Personnel Board and Deputy County 
Attorney. My opinions are mine alone.

that end, I am in support of your selecting Amourence Lee for mayor. Among the four of you, she is
the most senior at this time in terms of council experience and service. Continuity during this
transitional period is very important. Choosing her not only makes sense, but it's the right thing to
do for all residents of San Mateo.
Thank you for your consideration and again, congratulations to each of you on your wins.
Valerie Oblath

From: Genevieve Johnson 
 
Sent: Sunday, December 4, 2022 10:27 PM
To: City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org>
Subject: New Mayor of San Mateo, Council Member Lee
Sent from my iPhone Mayor Bonilla Council Members Goethals, Lee, Papan, and
Rodriguez, and Council Members-Elect Loraine, Diaz-Nash, and Newsom
I am writing in strong support of the selection of Council Member Amourence Lee as
San Mateo's next Mayor, at the City Council meeting on December 5, 2022.  Experience
matters and only Council Member Lee has it, having served the City well for the last
three years, after her appointment in 2019 and her election in 2020. As the only holdover
from the most recent council, she is the only Council Member who can provide
continuity, bringing an intimate awareness of past discussions on important issues.
The Mayor of San Mateo is an important position, setting the tone, leading the
discussion, and representing San Mateo in numerous regional bodies.
Mayor Lee would be the first Mayor of Asian descent in the City's history.  She would be
the first Mayor from North Central San Mateo in 20 years.
And finally, according to the City Council Handbook, Council Member Lee becomes
Deputy Mayor on December 4, with the resignation of Diane Papan (current Deputy
Mayor) from the City Council.  San Mateo custom has the Vice Mayor becoming the
next Mayor.
Please select Council Member Amourence Lee as Mayor of San Mateo!
413 of 417

Thank you,
Genevieve Johnson

Subject:
December 5th council reorganization and selection of mayor
Date:
Monday, December 5, 2022 2:12:04 PM
Dear esteemed council-members-elect Newsom, Diaz-Nash, and Loraine, and council member
Lee,
I’m writing to support the election of council member Lee as San Mateo Mayor at the
upcoming December 5th city council meeting. As someone who lives in North-Central San
Mateo, I'm incredibly proud to have Ms. Lee represent me. Her leadership has been incredibly
inspiring and makes me proud to have moved to San Mateo in the past year and I look forward
to her continued guidance as mayor elect. I know that she will be a strong leader and help our
city progress. 
Due to her tenure as the only incumbent councilmember, it is my understanding per city
council guidelines that she will be selected for this position, as befits her experience and
readiness for the job; so I expect the selection process itself to be a formality following
established conventions. As such, I am looking forward to celebrating her historic
representation of the Asian American community as our new mayor.
Thank you,
Alexandra Dove
San Mateo resident

From:
Rustard Mustard
To:
City Council (San Mateo)
Cc:
Clerk
Subject:
Selection of Mayor
Date:
Monday, December 5, 2022 3:53:56 PM
Dear Mayor Bonilla, Council Members Goethals, Lee, Papan, and Rodriguez, and 
Council Members-Elect Loraine, Diaz-Nash, and Newsom,
I am writing in strong support of the selection of Council Member Amourence Lee as 
San Mateo's next Mayor, at the City Council meeting on December 5, 2022. 
Council Member Lee is the only person that has experience being on the Council. 
There is a major transition period that comes between being a resident and becoming 
a Council member. There is also a heavy workload with all of the additional 
committees and boards.
Once again there is a steep learning curve going from Council member to Mayor. 
My grave concern is that there are major issues that the City is currently dealing with 
and without a steady hand at the City's helm, we could experience extreme chaos. 
Let us avoid that by appointing Amourence Lee as the Mayor. She is the only 
experienced choice.
Thank you for your time.
Sincerely,
Suzanne Bonilla
